COMPLETE MEJORES AMIGOS PLATFORM PROMPT FOR JULES (2M TOKENS)
You are tasked with building the complete Mejores Amigos platform – a private, friends-only web application that serves as a community hub for games, entertainment, and productivity. This is a sequel to the existing auction game; you will integrate that auction into a larger ecosystem. The platform includes:

1. A main entry page with name/password login (separate from auction admin).
2. A community hub with three sections: Games, Entertainment, and Padippi Area.
3. Games section: includes the existing football auction (linked), chess, tic-tac-toe, and placeholders for more.
4. Entertainment section: anime streaming with a custom video player (YouTube+VLC style), powered by a Telegram bot that indexes anime files into MongoDB.
5. Padippi Area: placeholder "in development" with study/work features later.
6. A powerful admin panel for the main app (not the auction) with user management, session logs, bans, etc.
7. Full integration with MongoDB for data persistence, Telegram bot for anime indexing, and Jikan API for metadata.

All code must be production-ready, deployed on Render, using Node.js, Socket.io (for real-time features like online indicators, chess, etc.), and vanilla JavaScript frontend (with the provided Claude UI as base). No frameworks like React.

Below is every detail, split into parts for clarity but all must be implemented.

====================================================================================================
PART 0: BASE UI FROM CLAUDE (PROVIDED)
====================================================================================================

You are given an HTML file (mejores-amigos-hub.html) that contains the complete UI for the hub. It includes:
- Header with logo, online friends bar, user chip.
- Navigation tabs: Games, Entertainment, Padippi.
- Games section with auction card, game grid (chess, tic-tac-toe, coming soon).
- Entertainment section with search bar, anime grid, episode sidebar, and video player.
- Padippi section with "In Development" placeholder.

You must integrate this UI with your backend. Replace static placeholders with dynamic data from MongoDB and real-time sockets. Keep all styles, animations, and interactions as designed; only add functionality.

====================================================================================================
PART 1: ENTRY & AUTHENTICATION (MAIN APP)
====================================================================================================

When a user visits the site (e.g., mejoresamigos.com), they see a login screen (replace the current header with a proper entry page). This is separate from the auction game's admin system.

LOGIN PAGE (index.html):
- Logo at top.
- Input field: "Enter your name".
- Button: "Join Community".
- If name ends with "admin" (case-insensitive), a password field appears.
- Password: "Devadutt@2011" (hardcoded).
- On correct password, user becomes main app admin (different from auction admin). They get a crown badge and access to admin panel.
- On incorrect password, error message.

After joining, user is redirected to hub (hub.html, which is the Claude UI). User's name and admin status are stored in localStorage and session on server (via socket). The server maintains a list of online users with their names, admin status, and last seen.

SESSION MANAGEMENT:
- Each user gets a unique socket ID.
- On disconnect, they are marked offline after a grace period (30 seconds). If they reconnect within 30 seconds, they are restored.
- If they close browser or click back, they leave immediately.
- The server tracks login timestamps and activity logs for admin.

====================================================================================================
PART 2: MAIN APP ADMIN PANEL (SEPARATE FROM AUCTION ADMIN)
====================================================================================================

Only users with main app admin status (password "Devadutt@2011") can access the admin panel. It is a separate page (admin.html) or a modal accessible from the header (only visible to admin).

ADMIN PANEL FEATURES:
1. User Management:
   - List all registered users (names, when they joined, last seen, total time spent on platform, number of sessions).
   - Ability to "Remove Session" for a user (force logout, clear their session).
   - Ability to "Ban User" – prevent that name from joining again (add to banned list in DB). Banned users see "You are banned" message.
   - Unban option.

2. Session Logs:
   - View logs of all user activity: login time, logout time, duration, pages visited, actions (like starting a game, watching anime).
   - Filter by user, date.
   - Export logs as CSV.

3. Anime Indexing Status (from bot):
   - See list of anime indexed, episodes count, missing episodes.
   - Trigger re-index or update from Jikan.

4. System Settings:
   - Change main app password (optional, but can be hardcoded for now).
   - View server uptime, active connections.

All admin actions are logged.

IMPLEMENTATION: Use a separate MongoDB collection "users" and "logs". Admin panel fetches data via authenticated API endpoints (with admin check middleware).

====================================================================================================
PART 3: GAMES SECTION
====================================================================================================

The Games tab displays:
- Featured card: FANTASY FOOTBALL AUCTION (already built separately). The card should have a button "JOIN WAITING ROOM" that links to the auction game's lobby (separate URL, e.g., /auction). The auction game is a separate app but must be integrated into the same domain (e.g., /auction/*). You need to ensure the auction game's backend and frontend work alongside the hub. Possibly run them on same server with different routes.

- Game grid:
  * CHESS: Real-time chess using Socket.io. Two players can play with invite system.
  * TIC TAC TOE: Same.
  * Coming Soon cards (grayed out).

CHESS IMPLEMENTATION:
- Use chess.js for game logic, chessboard.js for UI or custom board.
- Invite system: User clicks "INVITE" on chess card → generates unique link (e.g., /chess?game=xyz). Sends link to friend via WhatsApp. Friend clicks link → both enter chess room.
- Online indicators: show green dot when opponent is online.
- Full chess.com-like features: timers (choose time control), move history, resign, draw offer, chat.
- Use Socket.io rooms for each game.

TIC TAC TOE:
- Simple 3x3 grid.
- Same invite system.
- Turn-based with real-time updates.

Both games must be accessible only to logged-in users. Store game history in MongoDB (optional).

====================================================================================================
PART 4: ENTERTAINMENT SECTION & ANIME STREAMING
====================================================================================================

This is the most complex part. It consists of:

4.1 Anime Database (MongoDB)
Collection: "anime" with schema:
{
  title: "One Piece",
  title_lower: "one piece",
  jikan_id: 21,
  poster: "url from Jikan",
  synopsis: "...",
  type: "tv", // or "movie"
  seasons: [
    {
      season: 1,
      episodes: [
        {
          ep: 1,
          file_id: "telegram_file_id",
          title: "Episode title from Jikan or custom",
          duration: 1440, // seconds, from file or default
          subtitles: [
            { lang: "English", file_id: "sub_id" }
          ],
          audio_tracks: [
            { lang: "Japanese", file_id: "audio_id" }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  ]
}

For movies: type: "movie", seasons array may be empty or contain a single "episode".

4.2 Telegram Bot (Node.js, using node-telegram-bot-api)
- Bot runs on same Render server.
- Commands:

  /index <anime name> - start indexing a TV series. Bot stores current anime context.
  /index <anime name> /s<num> - for season 2, 3, etc.
  /movie <movie name> - start indexing a movie.
  /stopindex - stop current indexing session.
  /list - list all indexed anime with counts.
  /check <anime> - show indexing status.

Workflow:
- User sends /index "One Piece". Bot replies: "Indexing One Piece. Send first episode file."
- User forwards episode file from channel. Bot records file_id, asks: "Send last episode file (or /done if only one)."
- User forwards last episode file. Bot calculates range and marks all episodes between first and last as indexed (using Jikan to validate total episodes). Bot stores metadata: title, file_ids for first and last; for mid episodes, it generates placeholder entries (no file_id) – later user can fill gaps if needed.
- For seasons: /index "One Piece /s2" then send first and last of season 2.
- For movies: /movie "Jujutsu Kaisen 0". Bot asks for file. User sends one file, stored as movie.
- Bot also fetches poster and metadata from Jikan API (https://api.jikan.moe/v4/anime?q=One+Piece). Use rate limiting (2 requests per second). Store jikan_id and poster.
- Subtitles and audio: If user sends a subtitle file (.srt, .ass) after an episode, bot can associate it. Use caption in message to specify language. E.g., send subtitle with caption "English". Similarly for audio tracks.
- Bot must handle very long gaps (user may send first episode today, last next week). Use persistent context in database.

4.3 Website Integration
- Entertainment tab displays anime grid from MongoDB. Each anime card shows poster and title.
- Clicking an anime opens its detail: seasons list (collapsible), episodes list.
- Clicking an episode loads the video player with that episode's file_id.
- Video player (already designed in Claude UI) must:
  * Stream video directly from Telegram CDN using file_id: https://api.telegram.org/file/bot<token>/<file_path> – but need to get file_path via getFile API. Better to proxy through your server? No, direct streaming is possible using Telegram's CDN but requires resolving file path. Implement a proxy endpoint that fetches from Telegram and streams to client (to avoid exposing token). But this consumes server bandwidth. Alternatively, use a client-side library that can fetch via Telegram's API with token? Not safe. So create a /stream/:file_id endpoint that internally calls getFile and redirects to the CDN URL or streams. Use http-proxy or axios pipe.
  * Support subtitle tracks: load .srt from Telegram and display using video.js or native track.
  * Support multiple audio tracks: not natively supported in HTML5; either use separate audio streams or switch video source. For simplicity, we can provide audio language selection by switching to a different file_id (if multiple audio versions exist). Or we can use a library like videojs-contrib-quality-levels.
  * Player controls: play/pause, volume, fullscreen, speed, next episode, previous episode (if series). All must work.
- If no anime indexed, show "No anime available. Ask admin to add."

The header shows online friends with green dots. This is powered by Socket.io:
- On connection, server adds user to online set.

PART 7: DATABASE SCHEMA (MONGODB)
====================================================================================================

Collections:

1. users:
{
  _id: ObjectId,
  name: String, (unique)
  isAdmin: Boolean,
  banned: Boolean,
  createdAt: Date,
  lastSeen: Date,
  totalTime: Number, // seconds accumulated
  sessions: [
    {
      login: Date,
      logout: Date,
      duration: Number
    }
  ]
}

2. logs:
{
  userId: ObjectId,
  action: String, // e.g., "login", "logout", "play_chess", "watch_anime"
  timestamp: Date,
  metadata: Object
}

3. anime:
As described in Part 4.1.

4. games:
Optional for storing chess matches etc.

====================================================================================================
PART 8: API ENDPOINTS (EXPRESS)
====================================================================================================

- POST /api/login - with { name } (and password if admin). Returns user data and token (JWT or session cookie). Use express-session.
- GET /api/users - (admin only) list all users.
- DELETE /api/users/:id/session - admin force logout.
- POST /api/users/:id/ban - admin ban.
- GET /api/online - get online users.
- GET /api/anime - list all anime (public).
- GET /api/anime/:id - get anime details with seasons/episodes.
- GET /api/stream/:fileId - proxy to Telegram stream.
- GET /api/subtitle/:fileId - proxy subtitle file.
- WebSocket events for online presence, chess moves, etc.

Probably yes, using same session. But auction may have its own lobby; we need to pass user name from main app. Implement shared session via cookie.

You are a senior full-stack developer with expertise in Node.js, Express, Socket.io, MongoDB, Telegram Bot API, and vanilla JavaScript. Your task is to build the complete Mejores Amigos platform from scratch. This is a private friends-only web application that serves as a community hub with three main sections: Games, Entertainment, and Padippi Area. The platform must be hosted on Render, use GitHub for version control, and be ready for real-world use by a group of friends.

This is a sequel to the auction game that was already built. That auction game exists separately and must be integrated into this larger platform. The auction game has its own admin system with password "123456". The main platform has a completely different admin system with password "Devadutt@2011". These are separate and must not be confused.

The user has provided a Claude-generated HTML file with the complete UI design. You must use that UI as the base and add all backend functionality. Do not change the UI design unless absolutely necessary for functionality. Keep all colors, animations, transitions, and layout exactly as designed.

This prompt is extremely long and detailed. Read every word carefully. Nothing should be left for the user to figure out. Every feature, every edge case, every button, every scenario is described here. You must implement everything exactly as specified.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 1: PROJECT OVERVIEW AND PHILOSOPHY
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Mejores Amigos is Spanish for "Best Friends". This platform is built for a close group of friends who want a private space to play games, watch anime together, and eventually study together. It is not a public platform. There is no public registration. Only friends who have the link and know the culture can join.

The platform has three main areas:

1. GAMES AREA: Contains the fantasy football auction game (already built), chess, tic tac toe, and placeholders for more games coming later. Games are real-time using Socket.io. Chess must copy 100% of chess.com logic and interface. Tic tac toe is simple but must have invite system.

2. ENTERTAINMENT AREA: Contains anime streaming. The user has every anime file on Telegram. A Telegram bot will index these files into MongoDB. The website will display all indexed anime with posters from Jikan API. Users can click any anime, see seasons and episodes, and play videos with a custom player that has subtitle selection, audio track selection, quality options, and all controls like YouTube and VLC combined.

3. PADIPPI AREA: Currently just a placeholder saying "In Development". Later this will have study timers, pomodoro with friends, goal trackers, and productivity features. For now, just show the UI with coming soon message.

The platform has two types of admins:

- MAIN APP ADMIN: Uses password "Devadutt@2011". This admin can see all users, remove their sessions, ban users, unban users, view detailed logs of who spent how much time on the platform, and monitor everything. This admin is like the super admin of the whole community.

- AUCTION ADMIN: Uses password "123456". This is only for the auction game and has powers only within that game like starting auction, dismissing unsold players, etc. This is completely separate and already built.

When a user first visits the website, they see a login screen where they enter their name. If they type "admin" at the end of their name (like "ishanadmin"), a password field appears. They must enter "Devadutt@2011" to become main app admin. If they enter wrong password, they get error and cannot join as admin. Regular users just enter their name and join without password.

After login, the user is taken to the main hub which has the three tabs. Their name and admin status are stored in localStorage so next time they visit, they are automatically logged in. But they should have option to switch account.

The entire platform must work in real-time. When users are online, they should see green dots next to names in the friends bar. When someone joins or leaves, it should update instantly. When two people play chess, moves should appear instantly on both screens with no lag.

All data must be stored in MongoDB. Use Mongoose for schema modeling. The Telegram bot must run on the same Render server as the main app. It will listen to messages from the user in Telegram PM and update the database accordingly.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 2: ENTRY PAGE AND AUTHENTICATION SYSTEM
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a user visits the root URL (https://mejoresamigos.com), they should see a clean entry page. This is NOT the Claude UI yet. This is a separate page called index.html.

The entry page must have:

- At the very top, the Mejores Amigos logo. Use the logo URL provided earlier: https://encrypted-tbn0.gstatic.com/images?q=tbn:ANd9GcQl5O38UyupxU5PU6W5jXASsMVPWHyg6ylDIg&s. Display it prominently.

- Below the logo, a heading that says "Mejores Amigos - Friends Community".

- Below that, a single input field with placeholder "Enter your name".

- Below the input field, a button that says "JOIN COMMUNITY".

- At the bottom, two small links: "About" and "Help". These can link to simple placeholder pages or modals.

Now the important part: admin detection logic.

When the user types their name, the JavaScript on the page must monitor the input in real time. If the user types a name that ends with the letters "admin" (case insensitive), a password field must immediately appear below the name input. This should happen without page refresh.

For example:
- If user types "ishan" -> no password field.
- If user types "ishanadmin" -> password field appears.
- If user types "IshanADMIN" -> password field appears.
- If user types "adminishan" -> no, must end with admin.

The password field must have type="password" so characters are hidden. Next to it, a small "Show" button can toggle visibility but not required.

Below the password field, the JOIN button remains.

When user clicks JOIN, the system must validate:

- Name cannot be empty. Minimum 2 characters, maximum 20.
- Name can only contain letters and spaces. No numbers, no special characters except spaces.
- Name cannot be already in use by someone currently online. Check against active sessions in database.
- If password field was shown (because name ended with admin), the password must exactly match "Devadutt@2011". Case sensitive.
- If password is incorrect, show error message: "Invalid admin password" and do not proceed.
- If name is already taken by an online user, show error: "Name already in use. Choose another or wait for that user to leave."
- If name is banned (stored in database banned list), show error: "This name has been banned. Contact admin."

If all validations pass, the system must:

1. Create a user session in the database with:
   - name: the entered name (if admin, strip the "admin" suffix. So "ishanadmin" becomes "Ishan" with capital I. "rohitadmin" becomes "Rohit".)
   - isMainAppAdmin: true if password matched, false otherwise.
   - createdAt: current timestamp.
   - lastSeen: current timestamp.
   - socketId: the socket ID from connection.
   - online: true.
   - ipAddress: capture from request (optional but nice for logs).
   - userAgent: capture browser info.

2. Store the user info in localStorage on the browser so next time they visit, they are automatically logged in. The localStorage should contain:
   - name
   - isAdmin (boolean)
   - a session token (could be MongoDB _id or JWT)

3. Redirect the browser to hub.html (the Claude UI).

If the user visits the site again and localStorage has valid data, they should be taken directly to hub.html without seeing the login page. But there must be a way to switch account. Maybe a small "Not you?" link on the hub that clears localStorage and redirects to login.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 3: MAIN HUB - THE CLAUDE UI INTEGRATION
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The hub.html file is the one Claude generated. It has:

- A header with logo, friends bar showing online friends with green dots, and a user chip showing the logged-in user's name and avatar.
- Three navigation tabs: GAMES, ENTERTAINMENT, PADIPPI.
- When GAMES is active, it shows:
  * A large featured card for Fantasy Football Auction with details like "Next Auction: Today 9 PM", "3 players joined", and buttons for "JOIN WAITING ROOM" and "GENERATE INVITE LINK".
  * A grid of game cards: Chess, Tic Tac Toe, and two "Coming Soon" cards.
- When ENTERTAINMENT is active, it shows:
  * A search bar for anime.
  * A grid of anime posters (placeholder images in Claude UI, must be replaced with real data from MongoDB).
  * A sidebar that appears when an anime is selected, showing seasons and episodes.
  * A video player area that appears when an episode is selected, with all controls.
- When PADIPPI is active, it shows a simple "In Development" message.

Your job is to take this static HTML and make it dynamic by connecting to your backend. Replace all static content with real data from MongoDB and real-time socket events.

The header's friends bar must show actual online users. Use Socket.io to maintain a list of online users. When a user connects, broadcast to all. When they disconnect, remove them after a grace period. The green dots must update in real time.

The user chip should show the logged-in user's name from localStorage. If the user is main app admin, show a crown icon 👑 next to their name in the chip and everywhere else.

The GAMES section's auction card must show real data. The "3 players joined" should come from the auction game's lobby. You need to integrate with the existing auction game. The auction game is a separate app but must be accessible via /auction route. So when user clicks "JOIN WAITING ROOM", they should be taken to /auction/lobby or whatever the auction game's URL is. The "GENERATE INVITE LINK" button should create a unique link that, when shared, takes friends directly to the auction lobby. The link should include the inviter's name maybe.

The chess and tic tac toe cards must have "PLAY" and "INVITE" buttons. The INVITE button should generate a unique link that can be shared via WhatsApp. When the recipient clicks the link, they are taken directly to a game room with the inviter (if both are online). The PLAY button could start a game with a random online opponent or just go to a waiting area.

The ENTERTAINMENT section is the most complex. The search bar must filter anime titles from MongoDB. The anime grid must display all indexed anime with their posters from Jikan API. Clicking an anime should open the episode sidebar showing seasons (collapsible) and episodes. Clicking an episode should load the video player with that episode's file from Telegram.

The video player must have:
- Play/pause button
- Previous/next episode buttons (for series)
- Volume control with mute
- Fullscreen toggle
- Playback speed selector (0.5x to 2x)
- Subtitle selector dropdown (if multiple subtitles available for that episode)
- Audio track selector dropdown (if multiple audio tracks)
- Quality selector (if multiple quality versions - but for now maybe just one)
- Progress bar with seek ability
- Time display (current time / total duration)
- Settings cog with additional options

All controls must fade out when mouse is idle and fade in on hover, like YouTube. The player must be smooth and responsive.

The PADIPPI section just shows "In Development" with maybe some placeholder graphics. No functionality needed yet.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 4: SOCKET.IO REAL-TIME CONNECTIONS
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You must implement Socket.io for all real-time features. The server must maintain a list of connected users with their names, admin status, and current page.

When a user connects:
- Add them to the online users set.
- Broadcast to all clients: "userConnected" with the user's name and admin status.
- Update the friends bar on all connected clients.

When a user disconnects:
- Do not remove immediately. Start a 30-second grace period. This handles brief internet drops or page refreshes.
- If they reconnect within 30 seconds with the same name, restore them to online status.
- If 30 seconds pass with no reconnect, remove them permanently and broadcast "userDisconnected".
- During the grace period, show a yellow dot or "away" indicator maybe.

When a user changes page (e.g., from games to entertainment), send a "pageChange" event so others can see what their friends are doing (optional but nice).

For chess and tic tac toe, use Socket.io rooms. When a game invite link is clicked, both users join a unique room (e.g., game_12345). All moves, chat messages, and game state are broadcast within that room.

For the auction game integration, the auction game already uses Socket.io. To avoid conflicts, use different namespaces. Main app uses default namespace or "/main". Auction game uses "/auction". Ensure they can run side by side.

SECTION 5: DATABASE SCHEMA - COMPLETE MONGODB DESIGN
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

You must use MongoDB with Mongoose. Create the following collections and schemas:

COLLECTION: users

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  name: { type: String, required: true, unique: true },
  nameLower: { type: String, required: true, unique: true }, // for case-insensitive search
  isMainAppAdmin: { type: Boolean, default: false },
  banned: { type: Boolean, default: false },
  createdAt: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  lastSeen: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  totalTimeSpent: { type: Number, default: 0 }, // in seconds, accumulated across sessions
  sessions: [
    {
      loginTime: Date,
      logoutTime: Date,
      duration: Number, // seconds
      ipAddress: String,
      userAgent: String
    }
  ],
  ipAddresses: [String], // all IPs used
  userAgents: [String] // all browsers used
}

COLLECTION: logs

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  userId: ObjectId, // reference to users collection
  userName: String, // denormalized for easy viewing
  action: { type: String, required: true }, // e.g., "login", "logout", "play_chess", "watch_anime", "join_auction", etc.
  timestamp: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  details: { type: Object, default: {} }, // any additional data like gameId, animeName, episode, duration watched, etc.
  ipAddress: String
}

COLLECTION: bannedNames

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  name: { type: String, required: true, unique: true },
  nameLower: { type: String, required: true, unique: true },
  bannedBy: String, // admin name
  bannedAt: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  reason: String // optional
}

COLLECTION: anime

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  title: { type: String, required: true }, // exact title from user's list
  titleLower: { type: String, required: true }, // lowercase for search
  searchTerms: [String], // for better search, could include alternate names
  jikanId: Number, // from Jikan API
  posterUrl: String, // from Jikan API
  bannerUrl: String, // optional
  synopsis: String,
  genres: [String],
  status: String, // "ongoing", "completed"
  type: { type: String, enum: ["tv", "movie", "ova", "special"], default: "tv" },
  totalEpisodes: Number, // from Jikan API or calculated
  year: Number,
  rating: String, // e.g., "PG-13"
  seasons: [
    {
      seasonNumber: { type: Number, required: true },
      seasonTitle: String, // e.g., "Season 1", "Season 2", could be custom
      episodes: [
        {
          episodeNumber: { type: Number, required: true },
          title: String, // episode title from Jikan or custom
          telegramFileId: { type: String, required: true }, // the video file
          duration: Number, // in seconds, can be extracted from file metadata
          thumbnailFileId: String, // optional thumbnail
          subtitles: [
            {
              language: { type: String, required: true }, // e.g., "English", "Japanese", "Spanish"
              fileId: { type: String, required: true }, // Telegram file ID of .srt or .ass
              default: { type: Boolean, default: false }
            }
          ],
          audioTracks: [
            {
              language: { type: String, required: true },
              fileId: { type: String, required: true }, // could be separate audio file or same video with different track
              default: { type: Boolean, default: false }
            }
          ],
          qualityVersions: [
            {
              quality: { type: String, required: true }, // e.g., "1080p", "720p", "480p"
              fileId: { type: String, required: true }
            }
          ]
        }
      ]
    }
  ],
  movies: [ // for anime that are movies (standalone)
    {
      title: String, // e.g., "Jujutsu Kaisen 0"
      telegramFileId: { type: String, required: true },
      posterUrl: String,
      synopsis: String,
      duration: Number,
      subtitles: [ /* same as above */ ],
      audioTracks: [ /* same as above */ ],
      qualityVersions: [ /* same as above */ ]
    }
  ],
  indexedAt: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  lastUpdated: { type: Date, default: Date.now }
}

COLLECTION: animeIndexingQueue (for bot to remember where it left off)

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  userId: Number, // Telegram user ID of the person indexing (the user's)
  currentAnime: String, // anime being indexed
  currentSeason: Number, // season number, default 1
  currentType: { type: String, enum: ["tv", "movie"], default: "tv" },
  firstEpisodeFileId: String, // store first episode's fileId when waiting for last
  firstEpisodeNumber: Number,
  waitingFor: { type: String, enum: ["first", "last", "done"] }, // what we're waiting for
  createdAt: { type: Date, default: Date.now },
  updatedAt: { type: Date, default: Date.now }
}

COLLECTION: chessGames (optional, for storing match history)

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  gameId: { type: String, required: true, unique: true },
  whitePlayer: { type: String, required: true }, // user name
  blackPlayer: { type: String, required: true },
  timeControl: String, // e.g., "10+0", "5+3"
  moves: [String], // algebraic notation
  result: String, // "1-0", "0-1", "1/2-1/2"
  pgn: String, // full PGN
  fenHistory: [String], // position after each move
  startedAt: Date,
  endedAt: Date,
  winner: String, // user name or "draw"
  termination: String // "checkmate", "resignation", "timeout", "draw agreement"
}

COLLECTION: tictactoeGames (similar but simpler)

{
  _id: ObjectId,
  gameId: { type: String, required: true, unique: true },
  playerX: String,
  playerO: String,
  board: [String], // 9 elements, "X", "O", or null
  currentTurn: String, // "X" or "O"
  moves: [Number], // indices of moves
  result: String, // "X wins", "O wins", "draw"
  startedAt: Date,
  endedAt: Date
}

Make sure all collections have appropriate indexes for fast queries. For example, users.nameLower unique, anime.titleLower, logs.timestamp, etc.

SECTION 7: TELEGRAM BOT - COMPLETE SPECIFICATION
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The Telegram bot is critical for anime indexing. It must run 24/7 on the same Render server as the main app. Use node-telegram-bot-api library.

BOT SETUP:

Create a bot on Telegram via BotFather. Get the token. Store it in environment variable TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN. Never hardcode.

The bot will only respond to the user who owns the anime files. That user's Telegram ID must be stored in environment variable ADMIN_TELEGRAM_ID. The bot should ignore messages from anyone else (or just reply "Unauthorized").

BOT COMMANDS:

Command: /start
- Reply with welcome message and list of available commands.

Command: /help
- Show detailed help with examples.

Command: /list
- Show all anime currently in database with counts.
- Format: "1. One Piece - 1000 episodes (TV)"
- If many, paginate.

Command: /index <anime name>
- Start indexing a TV series.
- Example: /index One Piece
- Bot replies: "Indexing One Piece. Send the FIRST episode file."
- Bot stores in animeIndexingQueue: { currentAnime: "One Piece", currentSeason: 1, currentType: "tv", waitingFor: "first" }
- Bot also checks if anime already exists in database. If yes, warn and ask if want to overwrite or add episodes.

Command: /index <anime name> /s<number>
- Start indexing a specific season.
- Example: /index One Piece /s2
- Bot replies: "Indexing One Piece Season 2. Send the FIRST episode file."
- Bot sets currentSeason = 2 in queue.

Command: /movie <movie name>
- Start indexing a movie.
- Example: /movie Jujutsu Kaisen 0
- Bot replies: "Indexing movie: Jujutsu Kaisen 0. Send the movie file."
- Bot sets currentType = "movie" in queue.

Command: /stopindex
- Stop current indexing session and clear queue.
- Bot replies: "Indexing stopped. Queue cleared."

Command: /status
- Show what is currently being indexed (if anything).

Command: /check <anime name>
- Show indexing status for that anime: seasons, episodes indexed, missing episodes.

Command: /search <query>
- Search Jikan API and return matching anime with their MAL IDs.
- Useful to verify names.

Command: /settitle <anime name> <new title>
- Manually correct title if needed.

Command: /delete <anime name>
- Delete an anime from database (with confirmation).

BOT WORKFLOW FOR TV SERIES:

Step 1: User sends /index "One Piece"
Step 2: Bot replies: "Indexing One Piece. Send the FIRST episode file."
Step 3: User forwards or sends a video file. This could be from a channel or local file.
Step 4: Bot receives file, gets file_id. Bot replies: "First episode received. Now send the LAST episode file (or /done if this is the only episode)."
Step 5: Bot stores first episode file_id and episode number (if it can extract from filename, otherwise assume episode 1).
Step 6: User sends last episode file.
Step 7: Bot receives file, gets file_id. Bot now knows first episode = 1, last episode = X (extract from filename or ask user).
Step 8: Bot queries Jikan API to get total episodes for this anime. If last episode > total episodes from Jikan, warn user.
Step 9: Bot creates anime document in MongoDB (if not exists) and creates season 1 with episodes from 1 to X.
Step 10: For episodes between first and last, bot creates placeholder entries with no file_id? Actually the bot assumes all episodes exist. But user only sent first and last. So the bot marks all episodes as "indexed" but only stores file_ids for first and last. When user later sends missing episodes, bot can update.
Step 11: Bot replies: "Indexed One Piece Season 1 episodes 1-50. Missing episodes? Use /addmissing command."

Better approach: User must send every episode file? No, user said they will send first and last and bot indexes all in between. So bot assumes continuity. If there are gaps, user will need to fill later with separate command.

For missing episodes, create command /add <anime> /s<season> <episode> - allows user to send specific episode file.

BOT WORKFLOW FOR SEASONS:

When user sends /index "One Piece /s2", bot expects first episode of season 2, then last episode. Bot will create season 2 in the anime document.

BOT WORKFLOW FOR MOVIES:

When user sends /movie "Jujutsu Kaisen 0", bot waits for one file. Stores it in movies array.

HANDLING SUBTITLES AND AUDIO TRACKS:

User can send subtitle files (.srt, .ass) with caption specifying language. Bot must associate with the last indexed episode or allow specifying.

Example flow:
1. User indexes episode 5 of One Piece.
2. Later user sends subtitle file with caption "English".
3. Bot checks: was there a recent episode indexed? If yes, ask "Associate with which episode?" Or use a command: /sub <anime> /s<season> <episode> <language> and then send file.

Same for audio tracks.

HANDLING QUALITY VERSIONS:

User might have multiple quality versions (1080p, 720p). Use command /quality <anime> /s<season> <episode> <quality> then send file.

BOT MUST BE STATELESS? Actually it needs to remember context. Use MongoDB collection animeIndexingQueue to store current state. This survives bot restarts.

BOT RESPONSES MUST BE CLEAR AND FRIENDLY. Use emojis appropriately.

BOT MUST HANDLE VERY LONG DELAYS between messages. User might send first episode today, last episode next week. Bot must remember context indefinitely. Use updatedAt timestamp to eventually expire contexts after say 30 days, but for now keep forever.

BOT MUST VALIDATE THAT ANIME NAMES ARE FROM THE USER'S PROVIDED LIST. The user gave a massive list of anime names. Store that list in a separate collection or file. When user indexes an anime, check if it's in the list. If not, warn: "This anime is not in your master list. Continue anyway? (yes/no)" and wait for confirmation.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 8: JIKAN API INTEGRATION
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Jikan API (https://api.jikan.moe/v4) is a free API for MyAnimeList data. No API key required. Rate limit is 30 requests per minute and 2 requests per second. You must implement rate limiting to avoid 429 errors.

When indexing an anime, bot should:

1. Search Jikan: GET https://api.jikan.moe/v4/anime?q=One+Piece
2. Parse response. Usually the first result is the correct one. But sometimes there are multiple (e.g., "One Piece" vs "One Piece: Movie 1"). Use logic to pick the most relevant: matching title, type, etc. Or ask user to confirm with reaction buttons.
3. Extract:
   - mal_id (Jikan ID)
   - title (English or Japanese)
   - images.webp.image_url (poster)
   - synopsis
   - genres
   - episodes (total episodes if completed, or 0 if ongoing)
   - status
   - year
   - rating
4. Store these in MongoDB.

For ongoing anime, episodes total may be unknown. Use 0 and update later.

When user indexes episodes, compare with total from Jikan. If user indexes episode 500 but Jikan says total 1000, it's fine. If user indexes beyond total, warn.

Store Jikan ID to avoid duplicate lookups.

Implement a function to refresh metadata for all anime periodically (e.g., once a week for ongoing series).

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 9: VIDEO STREAMING IMPLEMENTATION
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This is critical. The video player must stream directly from Telegram servers without overloading your Render server.

Telegram file access works like this:
- Each file has a file_id.
- Bot can call getFile with file_id to get file_path.
- The full URL is: https://api.telegram.org/file/bot<token>/<file_path>

But you cannot expose your bot token to the client. So you must create a proxy endpoint.

Create endpoint: GET /api/stream/:fileId

Implementation:
1. Client requests /api/stream/abc123
2. Server checks if fileId belongs to an anime episode in database (optional security, but good to restrict to our content).
3. Server calls Telegram API: getFile(abc123) to get file_path.
4. Server constructs the full Telegram URL.
5. Server either redirects to that URL (302 redirect) OR proxies the stream.

Option A: Redirect (simpler, less server load)
- Server responds with 302 redirect to the Telegram CDN URL.
- Client then streams directly from Telegram.
- Disadvantage: Telegram URL is exposed. Anyone with that URL could access the file directly. But if the file is already public? Not ideal.

Option B: Proxy (more secure, but uses server bandwidth)
- Server makes a request to Telegram URL and pipes the response to client.
- Client never sees the actual Telegram URL.
- Disadvantage: all traffic goes through your Render server, which has bandwidth limits (500GB/month on free tier? Actually Render free tier has no bandwidth limit but CPU limits). Could be okay for small group.

Option C: Signed URLs (best but complex)
- Generate temporary signed URLs that expire.

For now, use Option B with proxy, but implement caching and range requests to support seeking.

The proxy must handle:
- Range requests (for seeking in video). Parse Range header and forward to Telegram.
- Content-Type headers.
- Caching (Cache-Control).
- Error handling (if file not found, return 404).

Use express and axios or node-fetch to pipe.

For subtitles, similar proxy endpoint /api/subtitle/:fileId that returns the subtitle file content with proper Content-Type (text/vtt or application/x-subrip).

For multiple audio tracks, you may need separate files. Stream similarly.

The video player in Claude UI must be integrated with these endpoints. When episode is selected, set video source to /api/stream/fileId. Subtitles can be added as <track> elements with src pointing to /api/subtitle/fileId.

Implement audio track switching by changing the video source to different fileId (if separate audio files) or using multiple audio tracks in Web API (more complex). For simplicity, assume each episode has one video file with one audio track. Subtitles are separate.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 10: CHESS IMPLEMENTATION - 100% CHESS.COM CLONE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Chess must be implemented exactly like chess.com. Use chess.js for game logic and chessboard.js for UI, or build custom board with SVG/Canvas.

Features:

10.1 Game Creation:
- User clicks "PLAY" on chess card -> goes to /chess page with options: "Create New Game" or "Quick Match" (if multiple online).
- User clicks "INVITE" -> generates unique link: /chess?game=xyz123&inviter=Ishan.
- When friend clicks link, both are taken to same game room.

10.2 Game Interface:
- Chess board in center.
- Above board: player names with clocks (white on left, black on right). Show green dot if online.
- Time controls: User can select before game: 1+0, 3+0, 5+0, 10+0, 15+10, 30+0, etc. + means increment per move.
- Move list on side (algebraic notation).
- Buttons: Resign, Offer Draw, Claim Draw (if applicable), Abort (before game starts).
- Chat box for players to communicate.
- Settings: Flip board, board themes, piece themes (optional but nice).

10.3 Game Logic:
- Use chess.js to validate moves.
- On each move, update board, check for checkmate/stalemate.
- Update clocks on server and broadcast every second.
- When player runs out of time, they lose.
- Offer draw: player clicks button, other player receives prompt. If accept, game drawn.
- Resign: game ends immediately.
- Threefold repetition, 50-move rule: implement automatic draw detection.

10.4 Invite System:
- Generate unique game ID (UUID).
- Store game in chessGames collection with whitePlayer, blackPlayer (null initially), status: "waiting".
- When second player joins via link, assign them as black and start game.
- If inviter specified white/black, respect that.

10.5 Spectators:
- Allow other users to watch ongoing games (optional). Show spectator count.

10.6 Game History:
- After game ends, show analysis board with move list.
- Option to download PGN.
- Save to database.

10.7 Real-time:
- All moves and chat via Socket.io rooms.

SECTION 15: FILE STRUCTURE
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Create this exact folder structure:

SECTION 16: SESSION MANAGEMENT AND SECURITY
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Use express-session with MongoDB store (connect-mongo). Store session data in database.

Session contains:
- userId
- name
- isMainAppAdmin
- loginTime

On each request, check if user is banned. If banned, destroy session and send to login with message "You have been banned".

On socket connection, authenticate using session ID from cookie (socket.io can share session via cookie-parser).

Implement rate limiting on login attempts (max 5 attempts per 15 minutes per IP).

Hash passwords? Only one password "Devadutt@2011" is used. Could store hash in env and compare. But for simplicity, direct compare with env var is fine since it's a static password.

For admin panel, add additional CSRF protection? Not critical for private app but can add.

All API endpoints under /api must check authentication. Admin endpoints must check isMainAppAdmin.

----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
SECTION 17: LOGGING SYSTEM
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Every important user action must be logged to the logs collection. This includes:
- Login, logout
- Joining a game
- Starting a game
- Watching an anime episode (start, stop, duration)
- Admin actions (ban, unban, remove session, etc.)
- Any errors

Logs help admin see who is doing what and troubleshoot issues.

When a user watches an anime episode, send periodic updates (every 30 seconds) to record watch time. On pause/stop, send final duration.

Implement a logging utility function:

logAction(userId, userName, action, details = {}, ip = null)


Call it everywhere.

SECTION 18: ONLINE PRESENCE AND FRIENDS BAR
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

The friends bar in header must show all online users with green dots. Clicking on a user could open a chat? Not required now but could be nice.

Implement using Socket.io:

- On connection, server adds user to onlineUsers Map with name, admin status, socketId, lastSeen.
- Broadcast to all "users-online" with the list.
- On disconnect, start 30s timeout. If no reconnect, remove and broadcast.
- On reconnect within 30s, cancel timeout and restore.

The friends bar UI must update dynamically. Use the Claude UI's existing friend avatar placeholders and replace with real data.

If many friends online, maybe show first 5 with a "+X more" indicator.

The search bar in Entertainment section must search anime titles in real-time (as user types) or on submit.

Use MongoDB text search or simple regex on titleLower. For better performance, create a text index.

Results update the anime grid dynamically.

When search is cleared, show all anime.

Log errors to console and to logs collection with stack traces for debugging.

Implement a global error handler for Express.

For Socket.io, handle errors and emit 'error' events to client.

Render expects a start script in package.json. Use:

Create a render.yaml or use dashboard. Set environment variables.

WebSocket support: Render supports it, but need to configure correctly. Socket.io may need to set transports: ['websocket', 'polling'].

For Telegram bot, Render may put the server to sleep after inactivity if using free tier. Use a monitoring service like UptimeRobot to ping every 5 minutes to keep it alive.

Alternatively, use a paid tier.

SECTION 25: TELEGRAM BOT - DETAILED COMMAND IMPLEMENTATION
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Now we dive deeper into the Telegram bot. This is one of the most critical components because without it, the anime section has no content. The bot must be robust, handle errors gracefully, and remember state even after restarts.

BOT INITIALIZATION:

Create a file called bot.js in the /bot folder. It should export a function that takes the Telegram bot token and MongoDB models as parameters. The bot should be initialized when the server starts.

```javascript
// bot.js
const TelegramBot = require('node-telegram-bot-api');
const mongoose = require('mongoose');

module.exports = function(token, models, adminId) {
  const bot = new TelegramBot(token, { polling: true });
  
  // Store models and adminId in bot instance for access in handlers
  bot.models = models;
  bot.adminId = adminId;
  
  // Set up command handlers
  setupCommands(bot);
  
  // Set up message handlers for files
  setupFileHandlers(bot);
  
  return bot;
};
COMMAND: /start

When user sends /start, bot should check if the user's Telegram ID matches adminId. If not, reply: "This is a private bot for Mejores Amigos. You are not authorized." and ignore further messages from that user.

If authorized, reply with:

🎬 Mejores Amigos Anime Indexing Bot

Welcome! This bot helps you index your anime files from Telegram into the database.

Commands:
/start - Show this message
/help - Detailed help with examples
/list - Show all indexed anime
/index <anime name> - Start indexing a TV series
/index <anime name> /s<number> - Index a specific season
/movie <movie name> - Index a movie
/stopindex - Stop current indexing session
/status - Show current indexing status
/check <anime name> - Check indexing status for an anime
/search <query> - Search Jikan API for anime
/settitle <anime name> <new title> - Correct anime title
/delete <anime name> - Delete anime from database

For more details on each command, use /help <command>
COMMAND: /help

If user sends /help without arguments, show brief help. If they send /help index, show detailed instructions for indexing.

Example:

/help index

To index a TV series:
1. Send: /index "One Piece"
2. Bot will ask for FIRST episode file
3. Send the first episode file (from channel or local)
4. Bot will ask for LAST episode file
5. Send the last episode file
6. Bot will index all episodes between first and last

For seasons, add /s2 etc: /index "One Piece /s2"

For movies, use /movie command instead.
COMMAND: /index

This is the most complex command. Implementation steps:

Extract anime name from message. Handle quotes for names with spaces. Example: /index "One Piece" should extract "One Piece". If no quotes, take everything after /index.
Check if anime exists in approved list (from SECTION 23). If not, reply: "⚠️ This anime is not in your master list. Approved list contains X titles. Continue anyway? Send YES to continue or NO to cancel."
Store a temporary context in the IndexingQueue collection: · userId: message.from.id · currentAnime: extracted name · currentSeason: 1 (default) · currentType: "tv" · waitingFor: "first" · firstEpisodeFileId: null · firstEpisodeNumber: null · createdAt: now · updatedAt: now
Reply: "📥 Indexing [Anime Name]. Send the FIRST episode file. This should be episode 1 (or the lowest episode number you have)."
If there is already an existing queue entry for this user, ask if they want to overwrite or continue.

COMMAND: /index

Same as above but set currentSeason to the number provided. Validate that season number is positive integer.

Example: /index "One Piece /s2" should set anime = "One Piece", season = 2.

COMMAND: /movie

Similar to index but for movies:

Extract movie name.
Check approved list.
Create queue entry with currentType = "movie", waitingFor = "movie".
Reply: "📥 Indexing movie: [Movie Name]. Send the movie file."
COMMAND: /stopindex

Clear any existing queue entry for this user. Reply: "🛑 Indexing stopped. Queue cleared."

COMMAND: /status

Show current queue entry if any. Format:

Current indexing session:
Anime: One Piece
Season: 1
Type: TV
Waiting for: First episode file
Started: 2024-01-20 15:30 UTC
If no session, say "No active indexing session."

COMMAND: /check

Query database for this anime. Show:

One Piece:
- Type: TV
- Seasons: 3
- Total episodes: 50
- Episodes indexed: 45
- Missing episodes: 6, 7, 8 (if any)
- Movies: 2
- Last updated: 2024-01-19
If anime not found, say "Not indexed yet."

COMMAND: /search

Call Jikan API: https://api.jikan.moe/v4/anime?q=query

Parse results and show top 5 with numbers:

1. One Piece (TV, 1999) - MAL ID: 21
2. One Piece: Movie 1 (Movie, 2000) - MAL ID: 456
3. ...

Reply with number to select or send more specific query.
This helps user verify correct title.

COMMAND: /settitle

Update anime title in database. Useful if Jikan title differs from user's naming.

Example: /settitle "One Piece" "One Piece (TV)"

COMMAND: /delete

Delete anime from database. Require confirmation: "Are you sure? This will remove all episodes and metadata. Send YES to confirm."

SECTION 26: TELEGRAM BOT - FILE HANDLING

When user sends a file (video document, video note, or video), bot must handle based on current waitingFor state.

FILE HANDLER LOGIC:

In bot.js, set up a listener for 'document' and 'video' messages.

Case 1: waitingFor = "first" (TV series)

Get file_id from message.document.file_id or message.video.file_id.
Try to extract episode number from filename. Use regex to find numbers. Common patterns: "Episode 1", "EP1", "01", etc. If multiple numbers found, take the smallest as likely episode number.
If cannot determine, ask: "Could not detect episode number. Please enter episode number for this file:"
Store file_id and episode number in queue: firstEpisodeFileId, firstEpisodeNumber.
Update waitingFor = "last".
Reply: "✅ First episode (episode X) received. Now send the LAST episode file for this season (or /done if this is the only episode)."
Case 2: waitingFor = "last" (TV series)

Get file_id.
Extract episode number from filename.
Now bot has first episode number and last episode number. Assume all episodes between exist.
Create or update anime document in database: · If anime doesn't exist, create new document with title, type="tv". · If season doesn't exist, create season array with seasonNumber. · For each episode number from first to last, create episode entry with: · episodeNumber · telegramFileId: only for first and last? Actually user only sent two files. So for middle episodes, set telegramFileId = null or a placeholder. User will need to fill gaps later. · Better approach: Create all episodes with null file_id, then later user can use /addeppic command to fill.
After creating, reply: "✅ Indexed [Anime] Season [X] episodes [first]-[last]. Total [count] episodes. Missing files for middle episodes? Use /addeppic command to add missing files."
Clear queue for this user (or keep for same anime? Could ask if want to add another season).
Case 3: waitingFor = "movie"

Get file_id.
Create or update anime document: · Add to movies array: { title: movieName, telegramFileId: file_id, ... }
Reply: "✅ Movie [Movie Name] indexed successfully."
Clear queue.
Case 4: No active session

If user sends file without active session, reply: "No active indexing session. Use /index or /movie command first."

ADDITIONAL COMMANDS FOR FILLING GAPS:

Command: /addeppic

Example: /addeppic "One Piece" /s1 24

Bot replies: "Send file for One Piece Season 1 Episode 24" User sends file. Bot updates that specific episode with file_id.

Command: /addsub

Example: /addsub "One Piece" /s1 24 English Bot replies: "Send subtitle file for One Piece S1E24 (English)" User sends .srt or .ass file. Bot adds to episode.subtitles array.

Command: /addaudio

Similar for audio tracks.

Command: /addquality

Example: /addquality "One Piece" /s1 24 1080p Bot replies: "Send 1080p file for One Piece S1E24" User sends file. Bot adds to episode.qualityVersions array.

For movies, similar commands but without season.

SECTION 27: TELEGRAM BOT - JIKAN API INTEGRATION DETAILS

Create a separate file /bot/jikan.js that exports functions:

// jikan.js
const axios = require('axios');
const BASE_URL = 'https://api.jikan.moe/v4';

// Rate limiting: simple queue with delay
let lastRequestTime = 0;
const MIN_INTERVAL = 1000; // 1 second between requests

async function makeRequest(url) {
  const now = Date.now();
  const timeSinceLast = now - lastRequestTime;
  if (timeSinceLast < MIN_INTERVAL) {
    await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, MIN_INTERVAL - timeSinceLast));
  }
  lastRequestTime = Date.now();
  try {
    const response = await axios.get(url);
    return response.data;
  } catch (error) {
    if (error.response && error.response.status === 429) {
      // Rate limited, wait longer
      await new Promise(resolve => setTimeout(resolve, 5000));
      return makeRequest(url); // retry
    }
    throw error;
  }
}

async function searchAnime(query) {
  const url = `${BASE_URL}/anime?q=${encodeURIComponent(query)}&limit=5`;
  return makeRequest(url);
}

async function getAnimeById(id) {
  const url = `${BASE_URL}/anime/${id}`;
  return makeRequest(url);
}

async function getAnimeEpisodes(id, page = 1) {
  const url = `${BASE_URL}/anime/${id}/episodes?page=${page}`;
  return makeRequest(url);
}

module.exports = { searchAnime, getAnimeById, getAnimeEpisodes };
When indexing a new anime, call searchAnime with the title. Take the first result (or let user choose via /search and /setid command). Store jikanId.

Then call getAnimeById to get full metadata: synopsis, poster, genres, total episodes, status, year, rating.

For ongoing anime, total episodes may be null. Set to 0 and update later.

Store poster URL in database. Use it on website.

PLAYER JAVASCRIPT:

Create a file /public/js/player.js that exports a Player class.

class AnimePlayer {
  constructor(videoElement, options = {}) {
    this.video = videoElement;
    this.controls = options.controls || document.querySelector('.custom-controls');
    this.currentAnime = null;
    this.currentSeason = null;
    this.currentEpisode = null;
    this.episodeList = []; // for next/prev navigation
    
    this.initEventListeners();
    this.initControls();
  }
  
  loadEpisode(animeId, seasonNum, episodeNum) {
    // Fetch episode data from API
    fetch(`/api/anime/${animeId}/season/${seasonNum}/episode/${episodeNum}`)
      .then(res => res.json())
      .then(data => {
        this.currentAnime = animeId;
        this.currentSeason = seasonNum;
        this.currentEpisode = episodeNum;
        
        // Set video source
        this.video.src = `/api/stream/${data.telegramFileId}`;
        
        // Load subtitles
        this.loadSubtitles(data.subtitles);
        
        // Load audio tracks info
        this.loadAudioTracks(data.audioTracks);
        
        // Load quality versions
        this.loadQualities(data.qualityVersions);
        
        this.video.load();
        this.video.play();
      });
  }
  
  loadSubtitles(subtitles) {
    // Remove existing tracks
    const existingTracks = this.video.querySelectorAll('track');
    existingTracks.forEach(track => track.remove());
    
    // Add new tracks
    subtitles.forEach(sub => {
      const track = document.createElement('track');
      track.kind = 'subtitles';
      track.label = sub.language;
      track.srclang = sub.language.substring(0, 2).toLowerCase();
      track.src = `/api/subtitle/${sub.fileId}`;
      track.default = sub.default || false;
      this.video.appendChild(track);
    });
    
    // Update subtitle dropdown
    this.updateSubtitleDropdown(subtitles);
  }
  
  // More methods: play/pause, seek, volume, fullscreen, etc.
}
STREAM PROXY ENDPOINT:

In server.js, add:

app.get('/api/stream/:fileId', async (req, res) => {
  const { fileId } = req.params;
  
  // Optional: verify fileId belongs to an episode in database
  const episode = await Anime.findOne({ 'seasons.episodes.telegramFileId': fileId });
  if (!episode) {
    return res.status(404).send('File not found');
  }
  
  try {
    // Get file path from Telegram
    const file = await bot.telegram.getFile(fileId);
    const url = `https://api.telegram.org/file/bot${process.env.TELEGRAM_BOT_TOKEN}/${file.file_path}`;
    
    // Proxy with range support
    const range = req.headers.range;
    const options = {};
    
    if (range) {
      const parts = range.replace(/bytes=/, "").split("-");
      const start = parseInt(parts[0], 10);
      const end = parts[1] ? parseInt(parts[1], 10) : file.file_size - 1;
      options.headers = { Range: `bytes=${start}-${end}` };
      res.status(206);
      res.set({
        'Content-Range': `bytes ${start}-${end}/${file.file_size}`,
        'Accept-Ranges': 'bytes',
        'Content-Length': end - start + 1,
        'Content-Type': 'video/mp4'
      });
    } else {
      res.set({
        'Content-Type': 'video/mp4',
        'Content-Length': file.file_size
      });
    }
    
    // Pipe the request
    const response = await axios({ url, method: 'GET', responseType: 'stream', ...options });
    response.data.pipe(res);
  } catch (error) {
    console.error('Stream error:', error);
    res.status(500).send('Streaming error');
  }
});
Similar for subtitles: /api/subtitle/:fileId returns the subtitle file content with proper Content-Type.

CHESS JAVASCRIPT:

// chess.js
const Chess = require('chess.js');
const ChessBoard = require('chessboardjs');

class ChessGame {
  constructor(gameId, playerName, isWhite) {
    this.gameId = gameId;
    this.playerName = playerName;
    this.isWhite = isWhite;
    this.chess = new Chess();
    this.board = null;
    this.socket = io('/chess');
    
    this.initSocket();
    this.initBoard();
  }
  
  initSocket() {
    this.socket.emit('join-game', { gameId: this.gameId, player: this.playerName });
    
    this.socket.on('game-state', (state) => {
      this.chess.load(state.fen);
      this.board.position(state.fen);
      this.updateMoveList(state.moves);
    });
    
    this.socket.on('move-made', (move) => {
      this.chess.move(move);
      this.board.position(this.chess.fen());
      this.updateMoveList();
    });
    
    this.socket.on('timer-update', (times) => {
      document.getElementById('white-time').textContent = this.formatTime(times.white);
      document.getElementById('black-time').textContent = this.formatTime(times.black);
    });
    
    this.socket.on('chat-message', (msg) => {
      this.addChatMessage(msg);
    });
  }
  
  initBoard() {
    this.board = ChessBoard('chessboard', {
      position: 'start',
      draggable: true,
      onDragStart: this.onDragStart.bind(this),
      onDrop: this.onDrop.bind(this),
      onSnapEnd: this.onSnapEnd.bind(this)
    });
  }
  
  onDragStart(source, piece) {
    // Only allow dragging if it's player's turn and they have the right color
    const turn = this.chess.turn();
    const pieceColor = piece.search(/^b/) ? 'b' : 'w';
    if ((turn === 'w' && pieceColor !== 'w') || (turn === 'b' && pieceColor !== 'b')) {
      return false;
    }
    if ((turn === 'w' && !this.isWhite) || (turn === 'b' && this.isWhite)) {
      return false;
    }
    return true;
  }
  
  onDrop(source, target) {
    const move = this.chess.move({
      from: source,
      to: target,
      promotion: 'q' // always promote to queen for simplicity
    });
    
    if (move === null) return 'snapback';
    
    this.socket.emit('make-move', {
      gameId: this.gameId,
      move: move
    });
  }
  
  onSnapEnd() {
    this.board.position(this.chess.fen());
  }
  
  formatTime(seconds) {
    const mins = Math.floor(seconds / 60);
    const secs = seconds % 60;
    return `${mins}:${secs.toString().padStart(2, '0')}`;
  }
}
SOCKET HANDLERS FOR CHESS:

In /socket/chess.js:

const chessGames = new Map(); // gameId -> { white, black, game, timers }

module.exports = (io) => {
  const chessNamespace = io.of('/chess');
  
  chessNamespace.on('connection', (socket) => {
    socket.on('join-game', ({ gameId, player }) => {
      socket.join(gameId);
      
      let game = chessGames.get(gameId);
      if (!game) {
        // New game, determine colors based on who created
        game = {
          white: player, // creator is white by default
          black: null,
          game: new Chess(),
          whiteTime: 600, // 10 minutes in seconds
          blackTime: 600,
          lastMoveTime: Date.now(),
          timerInterval: null
        };
        chessGames.set(gameId, game);
        socket.emit('game-state', { fen: game.game.fen(), moves: [] });
      } else {
        // Joining existing game
        if (!game.black && player !== game.white) {
          game.black = player;
          socket.emit('game-state', { fen: game.game.fen(), moves: [] });
          chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('player-joined', { white: game.white, black: game.black });
          
          // Start timer
          startTimer(gameId);
        } else if (player === game.white) {
          // White player reconnecting
          socket.emit('game-state', { fen: game.game.fen(), moves: [] });
        } else {
          socket.emit('error', 'Game is full');
        }
      }
    });
    
    socket.on('make-move', ({ gameId, move }) => {
      const game = chessGames.get(gameId);
      if (!game) return;
      
      // Validate turn
      const turn = game.game.turn();
      const player = (turn === 'w') ? game.white : game.black;
      if (player !== socket.handshake.auth.username) {
        socket.emit('error', 'Not your turn');
        return;
      }
      
      // Apply move
      const result = game.game.move(move);
      if (result) {
        // Update timers
        const now = Date.now();
        const elapsed = Math.floor((now - game.lastMoveTime) / 1000);
        if (turn === 'w') {
          game.whiteTime = Math.max(0, game.whiteTime - elapsed);
        } else {
          game.blackTime = Math.max(0, game.blackTime - elapsed);
        }
        game.lastMoveTime = now;
        
        // Broadcast move
        chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('move-made', move);
        chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('timer-update', {
          white: game.whiteTime,
          black: game.blackTime
        });
        
        // Check game end
        if (game.game.in_checkmate()) {
          const winner = game.game.turn() === 'w' ? game.black : game.white;
          chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('game-over', { winner, reason: 'checkmate' });
          stopTimer(gameId);
        } else if (game.game.in_stalemate()) {
          chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('game-over', { winner: null, reason: 'stalemate' });
          stopTimer(gameId);
        }
      }
    });
    
    socket.on('chat-message', ({ gameId, message }) => {
      chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('chat-message', {
        user: socket.handshake.auth.username,
        message,
        timestamp: Date.now()
      });
    });
    
    socket.on('disconnect', () => {
      // Handle player disconnect
    });
  });
};

function startTimer(gameId) {
  const game = chessGames.get(gameId);
  if (game.timerInterval) clearInterval(game.timerInterval);
  
  game.timerInterval = setInterval(() => {
    const now = Date.now();
    const elapsed = Math.floor((now - game.lastMoveTime) / 1000);
    
    if (game.game.turn() === 'w') {
      game.whiteTime = Math.max(0, game.whiteTime - elapsed);
    } else {
      game.blackTime = Math.max(0, game.blackTime - elapsed);
    }
    game.lastMoveTime = now;
    
    // Check timeout
    if (game.whiteTime <= 0 || game.blackTime <= 0) {
      const loser = game.whiteTime <= 0 ? 'w' : 'b';
      const winner = loser === 'w' ? game.black : game.white;
      chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('game-over', { winner, reason: 'timeout' });
      stopTimer(gameId);
    }
    
    chessNamespace.to(gameId).emit('timer-update', {
      white: game.whiteTime,
      black: game.blackTime
    });
  }, 1000);
}

function stopTimer(gameId) {
  const game = chessGames.get(gameId);
  if (game.timerInterval) {
    clearInterval(game.timerInterval);
    game.timerInterval = null;
  }
}
SECTION 32: TIC TAC TOE IMPLEMENTATION

Similar to chess but simpler. Create tictactoe.html with a 3x3 grid.

GAME LOGIC:

class TicTacToe {
  constructor(gameId, playerName, isX) {
    this.gameId = gameId;
    this.playerName = playerName;
    this.isX = isX;
    this.board = ['', '', '', '', '', '', '', '', ''];
    this.currentTurn = 'X';
    this.socket = io('/tictactoe');
    
    this.initSocket();
    this.renderBoard();
  }
  
  initSocket() {
    this.socket.emit('join-ttt-game', { gameId: this.gameId, player: this.playerName });
    
    this.socket.on('ttt-game-state', (state) => {
      this.board = state.board;
      this.currentTurn = state.currentTurn;
      this.renderBoard();
    });
    
    this.socket.on('ttt-move-made', (data) => {
      this.board[data.index] = data.player;
      this.currentTurn = data.nextTurn;
      this.renderBoard();
    });
  }
  
  makeMove(index) {
    if (this.board[index] !== '' || this.currentTurn !== (this.isX ? 'X' : 'O')) {
      return;
    }
    
    this.socket.emit('ttt-make-move', {
      gameId: this.gameId,
      index: index,
      player: this.currentTurn
    });
  }
  
  renderBoard() {
    // Update UI
  }
}
Socket handlers similar to chess but simpler.

const onlineUsers = new Map(); // socketId -> { name, isAdmin, lastSeen }

module.exports = (io) => {
  io.on('connection', (socket) => {
    // Get user from session
    const session = socket.request.session;
    if (!session.userId) {
      socket.disconnect();
      return;
    }
    
    const user = {
      name: session.name,
      isAdmin: session.isMainAppAdmin,
      lastSeen: Date.now()
    };
    
    onlineUsers.set(socket.id, user);
    
    // Broadcast updated list
    broadcastOnlineUsers();
    
    socket.on('disconnect', () => {
      onlineUsers.delete(socket.id);
      broadcastOnlineUsers();
    });
    
    // Heartbeat to keep connection alive
    socket.on('heartbeat', () => {
      const user = onlineUsers.get(socket.id);
      if (user) {
        user.lastSeen = Date.now();
      }
    });
  });
  
  function broadcastOnlineUsers() {
    const users = Array.from(onlineUsers.values()).map(u => ({
      name: u.name,
      isAdmin: u.isAdmin
    }));
    io.emit('online-users', users);
  }
};
In hub.html, listen for 'online-users' event and update friends bar.

SECTION 36: LOGGING SYSTEM - DETAILED

Create a middleware for logging API requests:

// middleware/logger.js
module.exports = async (req, res, next) => {
  const start = Date.now();
  
  res.on('finish', () => {
    const duration = Date.now() - start;
    
    // Log to database if user is authenticated
    if (req.session.userId) {
      const Log = req.app.get('models').Log;
      new Log({
        userId: req.session.userId,
        userName: req.session.name,
        action: `${req.method} ${req.path}`,
        details: {
          status: res.statusCode,
          duration,
          query: req.query,
          body: req.body // sanitize sensitive data
        },
        ipAddress: req.ip
      }).save().catch(err => console.error('Log save error:', err));
    }
  });
  
  next();
};
Also log socket events.

SECTION 37: BANNED USERS HANDLING

Create middleware that checks if user is banned:

// middleware/banCheck.js
module.exports = async (req, res, next) => {
  if (req.session.userId) {
    const BannedName = req.app.get('models').BannedName;
    const banned = await BannedName.findOne({ nameLower: req.session.name.toLowerCase() });
    
    if (banned) {
      req.session.destroy();
      return res.status(403).json({ error: 'You have been banned' });
    }
  }
  next();
};
Apply to all routes except login.

For socket connections, check on connection and reject if banned.

SECTION 38: SESSION TIMEOUT AND CLEANUP

Implement session timeout: if user is inactive for 30 minutes, destroy session.

Use a lastActivity field in session and update on each request.

Also implement periodic cleanup of stale sessions and offline users.

SECTION 39: ERROR PAGES

Create custom 404, 403, 500 pages that match the site theme.

SECTION 40: MOBILE RESPONSIVENESS

The Claude UI is already mobile responsive. Ensure all new pages (admin, chess, etc.) are also responsive. Use CSS media queries.

For chess on mobile, board may need to be smaller. Use viewport units.

SECTION 41: PERFORMANCE OPTIMIZATIONS

· Use compression middleware for responses. · Cache static assets with Cache-Control. · Implement MongoDB indexes for frequent queries. · Use socket.io rooms instead of broadcasting to all for game-specific events. · Limit anime grid to 20 items with infinite scroll or pagination. All anime must be there

Make sure to follow all instrucyions any quesrions then ask before coding start code

SECTION 42: TESTING DATA

For development, seed the database with some test users and anime. Provide a seed script.

SECTION 43: DEPLOYMENT CHECKS

Before deploying to Render:

Set NODE_ENV=production.
Use secure session cookies (secure: true, sameSite: 'lax').
Ensure MongoDB connection string uses proper credentials.
Test WebSocket connections with multiple clients.
Verify Telegram bot polling works on Render (might need to use webhooks instead of polling). Polling is simpler but may not work on some hosting. Render supports polling.
SECTION 44: FINAL NOTES

This is an extremely comprehensive specification. Every feature has been described in detail. You now have all the information needed to build the complete Mejores Amigos platform.

The code you generate must:

· Use Node.js 18+ · Use Express 4.x · Use Socket.io 4.x · Use Mongoose 7.x · Use node-telegram-bot-api · Use chess.js and chessboard.js · Be well-organized with separate files for routes, models, socket handlers, etc. · Include comprehensive error handling · Be secure (no exposed tokens, validate input) · Be ready to deploy on Render with a single click

Start coding now. Generate all files with complete code.
